scope="row">Website</th><td>\n<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.dorsetforyou.gov.uk/">dorsetforyou.gov.uk</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Christchurch</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/a\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;tide&#39;">a\xc9\xaa</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/t\xca\x83/: &#39;ch&#39; in &#39;China&#39;">t\xca\x83</span><span title="/\xc9\x9c\xcb\x90r/: &#39;ur&#39; in &#39;fur&#39;">\xc9\x9c\xcb\x90r</span><span title="/t\xca\x83/: &#39;ch&#39; in &#39;China&#39;">t\xca\x83</span></span>/</a></span></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Town" title="Town">town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Borough" title="Borough">borough</a> on the south coast of <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>. The town adjoins <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth" title="Bournemouth">Bournemouth</a> in the west and the <a href="/wiki/New_Forest" title="New Forest">New Forest</a> lies to the east. <a href="/wiki/Historic_counties_of_England" title="Historic counties of England">Historically</a> in the county of <a href="/wiki/Hampshire" title="Hampshire">Hampshire</a>, it became part of the administrative county of <a href="/wiki/Dorset" title="Dorset">Dorset</a> in the 1974 <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1972" title="Local Government Act 1972">reorganisation of local government</a>. Covering an area of 19.5 square miles (51&#160;km<sup>2</sup>), Christchurch had a 2013 population of 48,368,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> making it the fourth most populous town in Dorset, closely behind <a href="/wiki/Weymouth,_Dorset" title="Weymouth, Dorset">Weymouth</a> which has a population of 54,539.<sup id="cite_ref-lovemytown.co.uk_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lovemytown.co.uk-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Founded in the 7th century at the confluence of the rivers <a href="/wiki/River_Avon_(Hampshire)" class="mw-redirect" title="River Avon (Hampshire)">Avon</a> and <a href="/wiki/River_Stour,_Dorset" title="River Stour, Dorset">Stour</a> which flow into <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Harbour" title="Christchurch Harbour">Christchurch Harbour</a>, the town was originally named Twynham but became known as Christchurch following the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Priory" title="Christchurch Priory">priory</a> in 1094.  The town developed into an important trading port and was <a href="/wiki/Burh" title="Burh">fortified</a> in the 9th century. Further defences were added in the 12th century with the construction of a <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Castle" title="Christchurch Castle">castle</a> which was destroyed by the <a href="/wiki/Roundhead" title="Roundhead">Parliamentarian Army</a> during the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a>. During the 18th and 19th centuries <a href="/wiki/Smuggling" title="Smuggling">smuggling</a> flourished in Christchurch and became one of the town\'s most lucrative industries. The town was heavily fortified during <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> as a precaution against an expected <a href="/wiki/Operation_Sea_Lion" title="Operation Sea Lion">invasion</a> and in 1940 an <a href="/wiki/Airspeed_Ltd." title="Airspeed Ltd.">Airspeed</a> factory was established on the town\'s <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Airfield" title="Christchurch Airfield">airfield</a> which manufactured aircraft for the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a>.\n</p><p>The town\'s harbour, beaches, nature reserves and historically important buildings have made Christchurch a popular tourist destination attracting some 1.5 million visitors a year. <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_Airport" title="Bournemouth Airport">Bournemouth Airport</a>, an <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> which handles approximately 800,000 passengers a year, is located within the borough boundary at <a href="/wiki/Hurn" title="Hurn">Hurn</a>. The airport\'s <a href="/wiki/Industrial_park" title="Industrial park">industrial park</a> contains a number of <a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">aerospace</a> and engineering businesses and is one of the largest employment sites in Dorset. Christchurch is a popular destination for retirees and has one of the oldest populations in the country with 30 per cent of residents aged over 65.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Governance"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Governance</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Geography"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Geography</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Climate"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Climate</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Green_belt"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Green belt</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Demography"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Demography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Landmarks"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Landmarks</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Town_centre"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Town centre</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Castle"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Castle</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Priory"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Priory</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Place_Mill"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Place Mill</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Highcliffe_Castle"><span class="tocnumber">7.5</span> <span class="toctext">Highcliffe Castle</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Sports_and_recreation"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Sports and recreation</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Notable_residents"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Notable residents</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Twin_towns"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Twin towns</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">13.1</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">13.2</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Christchurch,_Dorset" title="History of Christchurch, Dorset">History of Christchurch, Dorset</a></div>\n<p>Christchurch was founded in approximately <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">AD</span></span>&#160;650 by <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionaries</a> sent to <a href="/wiki/Wessex" title="Wessex">Wessex</a> by <a href="/wiki/Birinus" title="Birinus">St Birinus</a>, the first <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Winchester" title="Bishop of Winchester">Bishop of Dorchester</a> (Oxfordshire). They settled on a stretch of raised land between the rivers <a href="/wiki/Hampshire_Avon" class="mw-redirect" title="Hampshire Avon">Avon</a> and <a href="/wiki/River_Stour,_Dorset" title="River Stour, Dorset">Stour</a> which carried people and their wares to and from market settlements such as <a href="/wiki/Blandford_Forum" title="Blandford Forum">Blandford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Old_Sarum" title="Old Sarum">Old Sarum</a> (near modern <a href="/wiki/Salisbury,_Wiltshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Salisbury, Wiltshire">Salisbury</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Stannard_1999_1_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stannard_1999_1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The harbour became one of the most important in <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Saxon</a> England as it was easily reached from the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continent</a> and boats could travel up the river Avon to Salisbury.<sup id="cite_ref-Stannard_1999_1_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stannard_1999_1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The town appears in the <i><a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_Chronicle" title="Anglo-Saxon Chronicle">Anglo-Saxon Chronicle</a></i> entry of 901 as <i>Tweoxneam</i> (Twynham) from <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a> <i>betweoxn</i> (between) and <i>\xc4\x93am</i> (rivers).<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In around 890 AD, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_the_Great" title="Alfred the Great">Alfred the Great</a> considered Twynham to be of such strategic importance that, with the threat of invasion by the <a href="/wiki/Danes" title="Danes">Danes</a>, he made it a <a href="/wiki/Burh" title="Burh">burh</a> and defensive walls were erected around the town.<sup id="cite_ref-Stannard_1999_3_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stannard_1999_3-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In 1094 a chief minister of <a href="/wiki/William_II_of_England" title="William II of England">King William II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ranulf_Flambard" title="Ranulf Flambard">Ranulf Flambard</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Dean_(religion)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dean (religion)">Dean</a> of Twynham, began the building of <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Priory" title="Christchurch Priory">a priory</a> on the site of the original mission church.<sup id="cite_ref-Taylor_1994_1_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor_1994_1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Soon after the construction of the priory the town became known as Christchurch.<sup id="cite_ref-Taylor_1994_1_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor_1994_1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ChristchurchCastle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/ChristchurchCastle.jpg/220px-ChristchurchCastle.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/ChristchurchCastle.jpg/330px-ChristchurchCastle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/ChristchurchCastle.jpg/440px-ChristchurchCastle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3039" data-file-height="2014" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ChristchurchCastle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Castle" title="Christchurch Castle">Christchurch Castle</a> ruins</div></div></div>\n<p>Some time in the early 12th century, a <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Castle" title="Christchurch Castle">castle</a> was built within the town.<sup id="cite_ref-Moxey_1997_pp._89\xe2\x80\x9390_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moxey_1997_pp._89\xe2\x80\x9390-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Originally a wooden fort built by <a href="/wiki/Richard_de_Redvers" title="Richard de Redvers">Richard de Redvers</a>, first cousin to <a href="/wiki/King_Henry_I_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="King Henry I of England">King Henry I</a>, it was rebuilt in stone by <a href="/wiki/Baldwin_de_Redvers" class="mw-redirect" title="Baldwin de Redvers">Baldwin de Redvers</a> to resist <a href="/wiki/Stephen_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Stephen of England">King Stephen</a> during the <a href="/wiki/The_Anarchy" title="The Anarchy">civil war</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Empress_Matilda" title="Empress Matilda">Empress Matilda</a>. The castle again saw action during the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">Civil War of 1642\xe2\x80\x931651</a> when occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Roundheads" class="mw-redirect" title="Roundheads">Parliamentarians</a>. Christchurch changed hands a number of times: originally under <a href="/wiki/Cavaliers" class="mw-redirect" title="Cavaliers">Royalist</a> control, it was captured by Sir <a href="/wiki/William_Waller" title="William Waller">William Waller</a>\'s Parliamentary army in 1644. <a href="/wiki/George_Goring,_1st_Earl_of_Norwich" title="George Goring, 1st Earl of Norwich">Lord Goring</a> briefly retook the town in 1645 but was obliged to withdraw and returned with a larger force days later and laid siege to the castle. However, the Parliamentarians withstood the siege and maintained their hold on the town. Fearing such a powerful stronghold might once again fall into Royalist hands, <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell" title="Oliver Cromwell">Cromwell</a> ordered the castle to be destroyed in 1652.<sup id="cite_ref-Moxey_1997_pp._89\xe2\x80\x9390_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moxey_1997_pp._89\xe2\x80\x9390-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stannard_p135/136_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stannard_p135/136-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although the fishing industry thrived in Christchurch, the importance of the harbour declined as it became inaccessible to vessels of a large draught. The harbour entrance was particularly troublesome with constantly shifting sandbars. In 1665 <a href="/wiki/Edward_Hyde,_Earl_of_Clarendon" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward Hyde, Earl of Clarendon">Edward Hyde, Earl of Clarendon</a>, bought the <a href="/wiki/Lord_of_the_Manor" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord of the Manor">Lordship of the Manor</a> of Christchurch. As part of his plans to improve trade in the town, he attempted to resolve the problems with the harbour entrance by cutting a new one through the <a href="/wiki/Spit_(landform)" title="Spit (landform)">sandspit</a> at the foot of <a href="/wiki/Hengistbury_Head" title="Hengistbury Head">Hengistbury Head</a>. However, upon completion the new entrance repeatedly silted up and in 1703 <a href="/wiki/Great_Storm_of_1703" title="Great Storm of 1703">a large storm</a> damaged a <a href="/wiki/Groyne" title="Groyne">groyne</a> which blocked the entrance entirely. Over the following 150 years alternative schemes were proposed but none were ever taken up.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hart%27s_Factory_Side_Elevation.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Hart%27s_Factory_Side_Elevation.JPG/220px-Hart%27s_Factory_Side_Elevation.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Hart%27s_Factory_Side_Elevation.JPG/330px-Hart%27s_Factory_Side_Elevation.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Hart%27s_Factory_Side_Elevation.JPG/440px-Hart%27s_Factory_Side_Elevation.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hart%27s_Factory_Side_Elevation.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hart\'s Fusee Factory, built in 1845. The manufacture of <a href="/wiki/Fusee_(horology)" title="Fusee (horology)">fusee</a> chains was an important industry in 19th century Christchurch.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Smuggling" title="Smuggling">Smuggling</a> was one of Christchurch\'s most lucrative industries during the 18th and 19th centuries due to easy access to neighbouring towns and the difficult harbour entrance which acted as a barrier to <a href="/wiki/Cutter_(boat)#Customs_services" title="Cutter (boat)">customs cutters</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hodges_2003_5_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hodges_2003_5-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Many townspeople were involved in this illegal trade and large quantities of wealth were accumulated.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In 1784 a confrontation between a gang of local smugglers and <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Customs_and_Excise" class="mw-redirect" title="Her Majesty&#39;s Customs and Excise">Customs and Excise</a> officers led to the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mudeford" title="Battle of Mudeford">Battle of Mudeford</a> in which a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> officer was killed and a smuggler subsequently executed.<sup id="cite_ref-Powell_1995_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Powell_1995-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Another important industry during this period was the manufacture of <a href="/wiki/Fusee_(horology)" title="Fusee (horology)">fusee chains</a> for watches and clocks. In 1790, Robert Cox began to manufacture fusee chains in workshops in the High Street.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> By 1793 Cox gained a monopoly on chain production in Britain, supplying watch, clock and <a href="/wiki/Chronometer_watch" title="Chronometer watch">chronometer</a> makers throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Moxey_1997_82\xe2\x80\x9383_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moxey_1997_82\xe2\x80\x9383-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In 1845 William Hart opened a similar factory in Bargates. However, by 1875 the chains were no longer required due to changes in watch designs and the factories were closed.<sup id="cite_ref-Stannard_1999_197_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stannard_1999_197-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The railway came to Christchurch in 1847 although the nearest station, Christchurch Road, was at <a href="/wiki/Holmsley_railway_station" title="Holmsley railway station">Holmsley</a> and passengers were taken the rest of the way by omnibus.<sup id="cite_ref-Taylor_1994_3_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor_1994_3-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In 1862 <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_(RC%26BR)_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Christchurch (RC&amp;BR) railway station">a new station</a> was built in the town close to where it stands today and was served by a branch line from <a href="/wiki/Ringwood" title="Ringwood">Ringwood</a>. Christchurch joined the mainline in 1883 and a <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_railway_station,_Dorset" class="mw-redirect" title="Christchurch railway station, Dorset">third station</a> had to be built.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Christchurch, and in particular <a href="/wiki/Mudeford" title="Mudeford">Mudeford</a>, had been enjoying a modest tourist trade since <a href="/wiki/George_III_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George III of the United Kingdom">King George III</a> had patronised the town in the 1790s but the arrival of the railways made Christchurch accessible to more potential visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-Hodges_2003_p._116_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hodges_2003_p._116-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Power_station" title="Power station">power station</a> was built in Christchurch in 1903 to power the public <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">trams</a>. The excess generated was sufficient to light the town and in 1940 it was added to the <a href="/wiki/National_grid_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="National grid (UK)">national grid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Moxey_1997_82_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moxey_1997_82-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:405fw-p47-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/405fw-p47-2.jpg/220px-405fw-p47-2.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/405fw-p47-2.jpg/330px-405fw-p47-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/405fw-p47-2.jpg/440px-405fw-p47-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="377" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:405fw-p47-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Republic_P-47_Thunderbolt" title="Republic P-47 Thunderbolt">P-47 Thunderbolt</a> of the <a href="/wiki/405th_Fighter_Wing" class="mw-redirect" title="405th Fighter Wing">405th Fighter Wing</a> at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Christchurch" title="RAF Christchurch">RAF Christchurch</a>, 1944</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1930, the Fisher Aviation Company began to provide flights from fields at the eastern end of <a href="/wiki/Somerford,_Dorset" title="Somerford, Dorset">Somerford</a> Road and by 1933 the company had flown over 19,000 passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In 1934 they obtained permission to establish an <a href="/wiki/Aerodrome" title="Aerodrome">aerodrome</a> on the site which became known as <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Airfield" title="Christchurch Airfield">Christchurch Airfield</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> During the Second World War an <a href="/wiki/Airspeed_Ltd" class="mw-redirect" title="Airspeed Ltd">Airspeed factory</a> was built on the airfield and began manufacturing aircraft for the <a href="/wiki/RAF" class="mw-redirect" title="RAF">RAF</a> and in 1944 the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Air_Forces" title="United States Army Air Forces">USAAF</a> <a href="/wiki/Ninth_Air_Force" title="Ninth Air Force">Ninth Air Force</a> established a base there. A <a href="/wiki/RAF_Hurn" title="RAF Hurn">second aerodrome</a> opened at <a href="/wiki/Hurn" title="Hurn">Hurn</a> in 1944 which  became <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_Airport" title="Bournemouth Airport">Bournemouth Airport</a>. In 1940, with the <a href="/wiki/6th_Army_(Wehrmacht)" title="6th Army (Wehrmacht)">German 6th Army</a> at <a href="/wiki/Cherbourg" class="mw-redirect" title="Cherbourg">Cherbourg</a>, Christchurch was fortified against an expected invasion:<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> the construction of <a href="/wiki/Bunker#Pillbox" title="Bunker">pillboxes</a>, gun emplacements and <a href="/wiki/Tank_trap" class="mw-redirect" title="Tank trap">tank traps</a> in and around the town, made Christchurch an "anti-tank island".<sup id="cite_ref-Hodges_2003_88\xe2\x80\x9394_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hodges_2003_88\xe2\x80\x9394-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Between 1941 and 1942 <a href="/wiki/Donald_Bailey_(civil_engineer)" title="Donald Bailey (civil engineer)">Donald Bailey</a> developed the <a href="/wiki/Bailey_bridge" title="Bailey bridge">Bailey bridge</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Military_Engineering_Experimental_Establishment" title="Military Engineering Experimental Establishment">Military Engineering Experimental Establishment</a> at Christchurch Barracks.<sup id="cite_ref-Stannard_1999_241_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stannard_1999_241-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Much development with a large increase in housing occurred from the mid-18th century. In 1873, 300 acres (120&#160;ha) of common land north of the town known as Portfield was enclosed and built upon and the town\'s population rapidly expanded.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> During the 20th century further development has seen the population grown from a little over 11,000 to more than 45,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Visionof2009_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Visionof2009-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In the 1950s a large housing estate was built to the east of the town centre and in 1958 a bypass was constructed which redirected traffic using the town\'s high street as the main thoroughfare to and from London and Southampton.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In 1974 the town was transferred from the county of <a href="/wiki/Hampshire" title="Hampshire">Hampshire</a> to Dorset following <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1972" title="Local Government Act 1972">local government reorganisation</a> and was granted <a href="/wiki/Borough_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Borough status in the United Kingdom">borough status</a> by a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Charter" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Charter">Royal Charter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hodges_2003_5_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hodges_2003_5-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Taylor_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Christchurch_Civic_Offices_-_Geograph_-_2025471.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Christchurch_Civic_Offices_-_Geograph_-_2025471.jpg/220px-Christchurch_Civic_Offices_-_Geograph_-_2025471.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Christchurch_Civic_Offices_-_Geograph_-_2025471.jpg/330px-Christchurch_Civic_Offices_-_Geograph_-_2025471.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Christchurch_Civic_Offices_-_Geograph_-_2025471.jpg/440px-Christchurch_Civic_Offices_-_Geograph_-_2025471.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Christchurch_Civic_Offices_-_Geograph_-_2025471.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Christchurch Civic Offices</div></div></div>\n<p>Christchurch is a <a href="/wiki/Non-metropolitan_district" title="Non-metropolitan district">local government district</a> which has <a href="/wiki/Non-metropolitan_district#Status" title="Non-metropolitan district">borough status</a>. It is the smallest of Dorset County Council\'s six districts and one of the smallest boroughs in England <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_districts_by_population" title="List of English districts by population">by population</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hodges_2003_5_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hodges_2003_5-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The district was formed by the merger of the Municipal Borough of Christchurch with part of <a href="/wiki/Ringwood_and_Fordingbridge_Rural_District" title="Ringwood and Fordingbridge Rural District">Ringwood and Fordingbridge Rural District</a> in 1974. Since then it has been part of the <a href="/wiki/Non-metropolitan_county" title="Non-metropolitan county">non-metropolitan county</a> of <a href="/wiki/Dorset" title="Dorset">Dorset</a>. It has some large rural areas including <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Bournemouth International Airport">Bournemouth International Airport</a> and the parishes of <a href="/wiki/Burton,_Dorset" title="Burton, Dorset">Burton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurn" title="Hurn">Hurn</a>. For <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Borough_Council_elections" title="Christchurch Borough Council elections">local elections</a> the borough is divided into 11 <a href="/wiki/Wards_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Wards of the United Kingdom">wards</a> <sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> containing 24 councillors. Elections take place every four years; the <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Borough_Council_election,_2015" title="Christchurch Borough Council election, 2015">last election took place in 2015</a> resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservatives</a> retaining overall control with 21 seats.<sup id="cite_ref-vote2015_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vote2015-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-highcliffe_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highcliffe-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The Mayor of Christchurch for 2015\xe2\x80\x932016 is Independent councillor Frederick F T Neale and the Deputy Mayor is Trish Jameson (Conservative).<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In existence since at least 1297, Christchurch\'s Office of Mayor is now mainly a ceremonial role with little power.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The Council Leader is Ray Nottage who has served as a Conservative councillor since 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Christchurch is represented by a <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Christchurch (UK Parliament constituency)">single parliamentary constituency</a> in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a>. The seat was created in 1983 from parts of the <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_and_Lymington_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Christchurch and Lymington (UK Parliament constituency)">Christchurch and Lymington</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Dorset_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="North Dorset (UK Parliament constituency)">North Dorset</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Forest_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="New Forest (UK Parliament constituency)">New Forest</a> constituencies. It had been held by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Adley" title="Robert Adley">Robert Adley</a> (Conservative) since its creation until his death in 1993. At the <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_by-election,_1993" title="Christchurch by-election, 1993">by-election</a> <a href="/wiki/Diana_Maddock" class="mw-redirect" title="Diana Maddock">Diana Maddock</a> <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">(Liberal Democrat)</a> was elected in one of the largest ever <a href="/wiki/Swing_(politics)" title="Swing (politics)">swings</a> (35.4%) against the sitting party.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The seat was retaken by Conservative candidate <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Chope" title="Christopher Chope">Christopher Chope</a> in 1997 and retained in 2001 and 2005. In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2010" title="United Kingdom general election, 2010">2010 general election</a>, Chope retained his seat with a considerable majority of 15,410 and 56.4% of the vote, making Christchurch one of the safest Conservative constituencies in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The Liberal Democrats won 25.3% of the vote, <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> 9.8% and the <a href="/wiki/UK_Independence_Party" title="UK Independence Party">Independence Party</a> 8.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Christchurch is part of the <a href="/wiki/South_West_England_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="South West England (European Parliament constituency)">South West England constituency</a> for elections to the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2018 the \'Future Dorset\' plan was approved by the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Housing,_Communities_and_Local_Government" title="Secretary of State for Housing, Communities and Local Government">Secretary of State for Housing, Communities and Local Government</a> <a href="/wiki/Sajid_Javid" title="Sajid Javid">Sajid Javid</a>, which means that Bournemouth, Christchurch and <a href="/wiki/Poole_Borough_Council" title="Poole Borough Council">Poole</a> borough councils will be merged into one singular <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth,_Christchurch_and_Poole" title="Bournemouth, Christchurch and Poole">unitary authority</a> in April 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Christchurch is the most easterly coastal town of Dorset and lies within the <a href="/wiki/Historic_counties_of_England" title="Historic counties of England">historic county boundaries</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hampshire" title="Hampshire">Hampshire</a>. The town abuts Bournemouth to the west and is approximately 9 miles (14&#160;km) east of <a href="/wiki/Poole" title="Poole">Poole</a>, 20 miles (32&#160;km) west of <a href="/wiki/Southampton,_Hampshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Southampton, Hampshire">Southampton</a>, 23 miles (37&#160;km) south of <a href="/wiki/Salisbury,_Wiltshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Salisbury, Wiltshire">Salisbury</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The town centre lies between the rivers <a href="/wiki/River_Avon_(Hampshire)" class="mw-redirect" title="River Avon (Hampshire)">Avon</a> and <a href="/wiki/River_Stour,_Dorset" title="River Stour, Dorset">Stour</a> which flow directly into <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Harbour" title="Christchurch Harbour">Christchurch Harbour</a>. The borough boundaries stretch to <a href="/wiki/Hurn" title="Hurn">Hurn</a> Forest in the north encompassing <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_Airport" title="Bournemouth Airport">Bournemouth Airport</a> and eastwards along the coast as far as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Walkford&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Walkford (page does not exist)">Walkford</a>. The River Stour forms a natural boundary to the west; the estuary and harbour form the southern boundary.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Christchurch_Harbour,_Stanpit_Marsh_and_Hengistbury_Head_-_geograph.org.uk_-_103551.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Christchurch_Harbour%2C_Stanpit_Marsh_and_Hengistbury_Head_-_geograph.org.uk_-_103551.jpg/220px-Christchurch_Harbour%2C_Stanpit_Marsh_and_Hengistbury_Head_-_geograph.org.uk_-_103551.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Christchurch_Harbour%2C_Stanpit_Marsh_and_Hengistbury_Head_-_geograph.org.uk_-_103551.jpg/330px-Christchurch_Harbour%2C_Stanpit_Marsh_and_Hengistbury_Head_-_geograph.org.uk_-_103551.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Christchurch_Harbour%2C_Stanpit_Marsh_and_Hengistbury_Head_-_geograph.org.uk_-_103551.jpg/440px-Christchurch_Harbour%2C_Stanpit_Marsh_and_Hengistbury_Head_-_geograph.org.uk_-_103551.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Christchurch_Harbour,_Stanpit_Marsh_and_Hengistbury_Head_-_geograph.org.uk_-_103551.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Harbour" title="Christchurch Harbour">Christchurch Harbour</a> with the Clay Pool (bottom right) where the rivers <a href="/wiki/River_Avon_(Hampshire)" class="mw-redirect" title="River Avon (Hampshire)">Avon</a> and <a href="/wiki/River_Stour,_Dorset" title="River Stour, Dorset">Stour</a> converge. <a href="/wiki/Stanpit_Marsh" class="mw-redirect" title="Stanpit Marsh">Stanpit Marsh</a> (centre left), <a href="/wiki/Wick,_Bournemouth" title="Wick, Bournemouth">Wick</a> (centre right) and <a href="/wiki/Hengistbury_Head" title="Hengistbury Head">Hengistbury Head</a> (top right). The thin line of beach huts at the top left reveals the position of <a href="/wiki/Mudeford_Spit" class="mw-redirect" title="Mudeford Spit">Mudeford Spit</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight">Isle of Wight</a> on the horizon.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Harbour" title="Christchurch Harbour">Christchurch Harbour</a> contains large areas of <a href="/wiki/Salt_marsh" title="Salt marsh">salt marsh</a> and is protected by a <a href="/wiki/Sandbar" class="mw-redirect" title="Sandbar">sandbar</a> known as <a href="/wiki/Mudeford_Spit" class="mw-redirect" title="Mudeford Spit">Mudeford Spit</a> which has fine sandy beach on both sides of a walkway lined with <a href="/wiki/Beach_hut" title="Beach hut">beach huts</a>. The harbour is protected by a natural <a href="/wiki/Headland" title="Headland">headland</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hengistbury_Head" title="Hengistbury Head">Hengistbury Head</a>) at the start of the sandbanks, and is a special site for <a href="/wiki/Sand_martin" title="Sand martin">sand martins</a> which nest annually in the sandy cliffs. The harbour is only accessible to shallow draught boats drawing up to 4 feet (1.2&#160;m) due to the sandbars at the entrance.<sup id="cite_ref-Christchurch_Harbour_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christchurch_Harbour-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The entrance, known as the Run, has Mudeford Quay on one side and the spit on the other. Considerable tides flow here: up to 6 knots (11&#160;km/h; 6.9&#160;mph) during <a href="/wiki/Spring_tide" class="mw-redirect" title="Spring tide">spring tides</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The harbour is a protected wildlife refuge and is home to large populations of <a href="/wiki/Swan" title="Swan">swans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wader" title="Wader">waders</a> and other bird life. On the south side, the harbour is enclosed by Hengistbury Head which was the site of the earliest settlement here dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Christchurch_Harbour_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christchurch_Harbour-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The landward end of the headland has a bank and ditch known as <a href="/wiki/Hengistbury_Head#Iron_Age" title="Hengistbury Head">Double Dykes</a>, built in about 700 BC, to protect the ancient settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Stanpit_Marsh" class="mw-redirect" title="Stanpit Marsh">Stanpit Marsh</a> is a 65-hectare (160-acre) <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserve" title="Nature reserve">nature reserve</a> situated just below the confluence of the Rivers Avon and Stour. During the 18th century it was notorious for smugglers landing tobacco and rum in the narrow channels of Christchurch Harbour.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> It contains areas of salt marsh and <a href="/wiki/Freshwater_marsh" title="Freshwater marsh">freshwater marsh</a> with <a href="/wiki/Reed_bed" title="Reed bed">reed beds</a> and is home to grazing horses, rare birds, and 14 species of rare or endangered plants.<sup id="cite_ref-Friends_of_Stanpit_Marsh_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Friends_of_Stanpit_Marsh-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> It was designated as a <a href="/wiki/Local_Nature_Reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Local Nature Reserve">Local Nature Reserve</a> in 1964 and a <a href="/wiki/Site_of_Special_Scientific_Interest" title="Site of Special Scientific Interest">Site of Special Scientific Interest</a> in 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>To the north of Christchurch is <a href="/wiki/St_Catherine%27s_Hill,_Dorset" title="St Catherine&#39;s Hill, Dorset">St Catherine\'s Hill</a>, the highest part of the borough at 53 metres (174&#160;ft) above <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-St.C_hill_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-St.C_hill-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> This hill is the most southerly of a chain of three hills, some 3 miles (4.8&#160;km) long with 35-hectare (86-acre) area of <a href="/wiki/Heathland" class="mw-redirect" title="Heathland">heathland</a> and coniferous forest. The <a href="/wiki/New_Forest" title="New Forest">New Forest</a>, Christchurch Priory, Hengistbury Head, <a href="/wiki/River_Avon_(Hampshire)" class="mw-redirect" title="River Avon (Hampshire)">Avon Valley</a>, Christchurch Bay, <a href="/wiki/The_Solent" class="mw-redirect" title="The Solent">The Solent</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Needles" title="The Needles">The Needles</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight">Isle of Wight</a> can be seen from viewpoints on the east side of the Hill. Stour Valley way, <a href="/wiki/Poole_Bay" title="Poole Bay">Poole Bay</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Purbeck" title="Isle of Purbeck">Isle of Purbeck</a> can be viewed from the south west side of the Hill. Due to its commanding views, St. Catherine\'s Hill has been in use since prehistoric times as a look-out area and beacon and in more recent years served as a military training ground.<sup id="cite_ref-St.C_hill_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-St.C_hill-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The hill is home to protected and rare wildlife species including the <a href="/wiki/Dartford_warbler" title="Dartford warbler">Dartford warbler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nightjar" title="Nightjar">nightjar</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Sand_lizard" title="Sand lizard">sand lizard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The geology of the borough is unremarkable; the <a href="/wiki/Bedrock" title="Bedrock">bedrock</a> is mainly composed of <a href="/wiki/Sand" title="Sand">sand</a> with patches of <a href="/wiki/Clay" title="Clay">clay</a> to the east and west, and superficial deposits (<a href="/wiki/Drift_(geology)" title="Drift (geology)">drift</a>) of sand and <a href="/wiki/Gravel" title="Gravel">gravel</a> cover the entire area.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The extraction of sand and gravel for construction purposes is carried out in the borough and the opening of more sites is planned.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Christchurch, like the rest of the country, has a <a href="/wiki/Temperate" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperate">temperate</a> climate with a small variation in daily and annual temperatures. The presence of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a> ensures that the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a> maintain an all-year-round ambient temperature, and, because of its position on the south coast of England, Christchurch has slightly warmer winters and cooler summers than settlements further inland. The warmest months in Christchurch are July and August, which have an average <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_temperature" title="Atmospheric temperature">temperature range</a> of 12 to 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (54 to 72&#160;\xc2\xb0F), and the coolest months are January and February, which have a range of 2 to 8.3&#160;\xc2\xb0C (35.6 to 46.9&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-annualweather_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annualweather-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The average annual rainfall of 594.5 millimetres (23.41&#160;in) is well below the UK average of 1,126 millimetres (44.3&#160;in).<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%; color:#000000;">75.3<br /> (2.965)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #9494FF; color:#000000;">69.0<br /> (2.717)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #9A9AFF; color:#000000;">67.2<br /> (2.646)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #B3B3FF; color:#000000; border-left-width:medium">594.5<br /> (23.406)\n</td></tr>\n\n\n\n\n<tr>\n<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">Source: MSN<sup id="cite_ref-annualweather_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annualweather-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_belt">Green belt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Green belt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/South_West_Hampshire/South_East_Dorset_Green_Belt" title="South West Hampshire/South East Dorset Green Belt">South West Hampshire/South East Dorset Green Belt</a></div>\n<p>Christchurch lies at the centre of a <a href="/wiki/Green_belt_(United_Kingdom)" title="Green belt (United Kingdom)">green belt</a> region that extends into the wider surrounding counties. It is in place to reduce <a href="/wiki/Urban_sprawl" title="Urban sprawl">urban sprawl</a>, prevent the towns in the South East Dorset conurbation from further convergence, protect the identity of outlying communities, and preserve nearby countryside. This is achieved by restricting inappropriate development within the designated areas, and imposing stricter conditions on permitted building.<sup id="cite_ref-green-belt_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-green-belt-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The area is 3,477 hectares (34.77&#160;km<sup>2</sup>; 13.42&#160;sq&#160;mi) (2010) in size,<sup id="cite_ref-green-belt_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-green-belt-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> and lies mainly to the north of the district, with portions surrounding the fringes of the Christchurch/Highcliffe-on-Sea urban area. Suburbs also excluded are Jumpers Common, the built up area of Burton, as well as Bournemouth Airport, with the rest of the borough including the rural portions and hamlets in the Hurn and Burton parishes being \'washed over\' by the green belt.\n</p><p>Landscape features and greenfield facilities within include the rivers Stour, <a href="/wiki/Moors_River" title="Moors River">Moors</a>, Avon and their <a href="/wiki/Floodplains" class="mw-redirect" title="Floodplains">floodplains</a>, Christchurch Priory, Chapel Lane solar farm, Blackwater and St Catherine\'s hills, Hurn Forest, Stanpit Marsh, Mudeford Spit, and the <a href="/wiki/Adventure_Wonderland" title="Adventure Wonderland">Adventure Wonderland</a> theme park. The <a href="/wiki/New_Forest_National_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="New Forest National Park">New Forest National Park</a> in Hampshire borders the green belt to the east of the borough in Burton parish.<sup id="cite_ref-green-belt_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-green-belt-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="toc" border="1" style="float:right; border-collapse:collapse; margin-right:10pt; margin-top:1em;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Age</th>\n<th>Percentage<sup id="cite_ref-dorsetforyou_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dorsetforyou-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>0\xe2\x80\x9315</td>\n<td align="right">15.8\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>16\xe2\x80\x9317</td>\n<td align="right">2.0\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>18\xe2\x80\x9344</td>\n<td align="right">27.1\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>45\xe2\x80\x9359</td>\n<td align="right">19.1\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>60\xe2\x80\x9384</td>\n<td align="right">31.9\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>85+</td>\n<td align="right">4.1\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Christchurch has a population of 45,080 according to a 2007 census, making it the fourth most populous settlement in Dorset.<sup id="cite_ref-2005profile_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2005profile-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> It lies in the <a href="/wiki/South_East_Dorset_conurbation" title="South East Dorset conurbation">South East Dorset conurbation</a> which is one of the South Coast\'s major urban areas with a total population of over 400,000.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Over the three decades between 1971 and 2001, Christchurch\'s population increased by 32% from 33,768 to 44,865; and between 1991 and 2001 by 8.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-Christchurch_Borough_Council_23_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christchurch_Borough_Council_23-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> This was more than three times the average for England and Wales (2.5%), and it is expected to grow by a further 16% to 52,100 by 2028.<sup id="cite_ref-Christchurch_Borough_Council_23_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christchurch_Borough_Council_23-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Christchurch_Borough_Council_6_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christchurch_Borough_Council_6-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Between 1999 and 2006 there was a net gain of 4,200 people from migration alone (i.e. excluding births and deaths).<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> On average 3,100 people enter the borough and 2,500 leave each year, giving a net average gain of 600 migrants.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> of Christchurch is four times the UK average with 873 people per square kilometre (2,307 per sq mi).<sup id="cite_ref-Christchurch_Borough_Council_6_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christchurch_Borough_Council_6-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Christchurch has one of the oldest populations in the country with significant proportion of residents wealthy senior citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-2005profile_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2005profile-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The percentage of the population aged over 65 in Christchurch is 30.4%, almost double the national average of 16.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-aging_population_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aging_population-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Highcliffe" title="Highcliffe">Highcliffe</a> on the borough\'s eastern boundary possesses the highest percentage of elderly residents in the entire United Kingdom at 69%.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Office_for_National_Statistics" title="Office for National Statistics">Office for National Statistics</a> predicted that by 2031, the percentage of residents over 65 will rise to 37.9.<sup id="cite_ref-aging_population_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aging_population-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In 2005, the life expectancy of female residents was 83.4 years and male residents 79.7 years. This was an increase on ten years previous (1995) when the life expectancy was 82.6 years and 77.0 years for females and males respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In common with the rest of Dorset, Christchurch has low numbers of black and minority ethnic groups: the vast majority (96.83%) consider themselves to be <a href="/wiki/White_British" title="White British">White British</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Other white groups account for a further 2.09% and those of mixed race 0.44%. Asian and <a href="/wiki/British_Asian" title="British Asian">British Asian</a> make up the next largest group with 0.25% of the local population, followed by Chinese, 0.16%, black, 0.13% and 0.11% from other ethnic groups.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Over 55% of the economically active population are in full-time employment; a further 22% work on a part-time basis.<sup id="cite_ref-Dorset_County_Council_2005_4_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dorset_County_Council_2005_4-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Of those in employment, over 40% of the borough\'s residents have a high skill level occupation and 17% have a low level one.<sup id="cite_ref-Dorset_County_Council_2005_4_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dorset_County_Council_2005_4-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Some 28.18% have no formal qualifications but 16.63% have a level 4 qualification or above (<a href="/wiki/Academic_degree" title="Academic degree">first or higher degree</a>, <a href="/wiki/Higher_National_Certificate" title="Higher National Certificate">HNC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Higher_National_Diploma" title="Higher National Diploma">HND</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Vocational_Qualification" title="National Vocational Qualification">NVQ levels 4 or 5</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Christchurch contains around 22,800 properties.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\nIn 2005 the average price of a detached house in Christchurch was \xc2\xa3323,416.<sup id="cite_ref-Christchurch_Borough_Council_5_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christchurch_Borough_Council_5-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> On average property in Christchurch is 24% more expensive than anywhere else in England and Wales.<sup id="cite_ref-Christchurch_Borough_Council_10_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christchurch_Borough_Council_10-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Nearly 80% of residences are owner occupied, 3% are vacant and a further 3% are second homes.<sup id="cite_ref-2005profile_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2005profile-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The borough has around 25,000 cars: an average of 1.21 per household.<sup id="cite_ref-Christchurch_Borough_Council_10_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christchurch_Borough_Council_10-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Christchurch, in common with the rest of Dorset, has lower crime rates than average for the UK. Reported crime rates per 1,000 of the population in 2006 (with figures for 2001 in brackets) are as follows: violence against the person 10.4 (4.8), sexual offences 0.7 (0.3), robbery 0.2 (0.3), burglary 2.2 (4.0), theft of vehicles 0.9 (2.5), theft from vehicles 3.6 (7.2).<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<center>\n<table class="wikitable" style="font-size:85%; width:70%; border:0; text-align:center; line-height:120%;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td colspan="12" style="text-align:center;"><b>Historical population of color:black;">41,240\n</td>\n<td style="background:#fff; color:black;">44,869\n</td>\n<td style="background:#fff; color:black;">\xe2\x80\x93\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="12" style="text-align:center;font-size:90%;"><small>\n</small><p><small>Census: 1801&#160;&#8211;&#32;2001<sup id="cite_ref-Visionof2009_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Visionof2009-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup></small>\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</center>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:right;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Sector\n<p><sup id="cite_ref-Dale_Jayne,_Gray_Anne,_Wicks_John_23_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dale_Jayne,_Gray_Anne,_Wicks_John_23-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</th>\n<th>2000\n</th>\n<th>2004\n</th>\n<th>2007\n</th>\n<th>Change\n<p>(\xc2\xa3M)\n</p>\n</th>\n<th>Change\n<p>(%)\n</p>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Agriculture\n</td>\n<td>10.5\n</td>\n<td>14.6\n</td>\n<td>16.3\n</td>\n<td>5.9\n</td>\n<td>56%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Mining/Quarrying\n</td>\n<td>0.0\n</td>\n<td>0.0\n</td>\n<td>0.0\n</td>\n<td>0.0\n</td>\n<td>0.0%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Food/Textiles/Wood\n</td>\n<td>6.9\n</td>\n<td>4.3\n</td>\n<td>4.0\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x88\x922.9\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x88\x9242%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Printing nes\n</td>\n<td>3.5\n</td>\n<td>4.7\n</td>\n<td>3.2\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x88\x920.3\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x88\x928%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Electricity/Gas/Water\n</td>\n<td>12.5\n</td>\n<td>14.9\n</td>\n<td>20.7\n</td>\n<td>8.2\n</td>\n<td>66%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Construction\n</td>\n<td>34.7\n</td>\n<td>49.6\n</td>\n<td>43.5\n</td>\n<td>8.8\n</td>\n<td>25%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Distribution\n</td>\n<td>73.5\n</td>\n<td>104.2\n</td>\n<td>110.8\n</td>\n<td>37.4\n</td>\n<td>51%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Hotel and Catering\n</td>\n<td>21.5\n</td>\n<td>27.0\n</td>\n<td>34.3\n</td>\n<td>12.8\n</td>\n<td>60%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Transport and Communications\n</td>\n<td>80.5\n</td>\n<td>119.9\n</td>\n<td>145.1\n</td>\n<td>64.6\n</td>\n<td>80%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Banking and Insurance\n</td>\n<td>15.2\n</td>\n<td>20.1\n</td>\n<td>25.5\n</td>\n<td>10.3\n</td>\n<td>68%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Other business services\n</td>\n<td>57.8\n</td>\n<td>56.2\n</td>\n<td>84.8\n</td>\n<td>27.0\n</td>\n<td>47%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Public administration and
