Health\n</td>\n<td>67.2\n</td>\n<td>70.7\n</td>\n<td>76.8\n</td>\n<td>9.6\n</td>\n<td>14%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Miscellaneous services\n</td>\n<td>22.9\n</td>\n<td>20.4\n</td>\n<td>22.3\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x88\x920.6\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x88\x922%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Total GVA\n</th>\n<th>552.5\n</th>\n<th>664.5\n</th>\n<th>757.0\n</th>\n<th>204.5\n</th>\n<th>37%\n</th></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Between 2000 and 2007 the total <a href="/wiki/Gross_Value_Added" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross Value Added">Gross Value Added</a> (GVA) of the borough grew by 37% from \xc2\xa3552&#160;million to \xc2\xa3757&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The biggest contributor to the local economy through the period 2000\xe2\x80\x932007 was the transport and communication sector which in 2007 brought in \xc2\xa3145&#160;million GVA; \xc2\xa364&#160;million more than in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-GVA_p.20_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GVA_p.20-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The sector which saw the largest growth during that period however, was metals and engineering which increased by 140%.<sup id="cite_ref-GVA_p.20_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GVA_p.20-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The food, textiles and wood industries experienced the largest negative change at \xe2\x88\x9242% whereas the electronics industry experienced the biggest fall with \xc2\xa316.2&#160;million less than seven years previous.<sup id="cite_ref-Dale_Jayne,_Gray_Anne,_Wicks_John_23_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dale_Jayne,_Gray_Anne,_Wicks_John_23-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An aircraft manufacturing industry was established in the town with the construction of an <a href="/wiki/Airspeed_Ltd." title="Airspeed Ltd.">Airspeed</a> factory at <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Airfield" title="Christchurch Airfield">Christchurch Airfield</a> in 1942. In 1948 the factory became part of <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland" title="De Havilland">de Havilland</a> and manufactured a wide range of aircraft such as the <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Vampire" title="De Havilland Vampire">Vampire</a>, <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Sea_Venom" title="De Havilland Sea Venom">Sea Venom</a> and <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Sea_Vixen" title="De Havilland Sea Vixen">Sea Vixen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In the 1950s, <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_Airport" title="Bournemouth Airport">Bournemouth Airport</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/RAF_Hurn" title="RAF Hurn">RAF base</a> situated on the outskirts of borough boundaries at <a href="/wiki/Hurn" title="Hurn">Hurn</a>, also became heavily involved in aircraft production after <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Armstrong" class="mw-redirect" title="Vickers Armstrong">Vickers Armstrong</a>\xe2\x80\x94which later became the <a href="/wiki/British_Aircraft_Corporation" title="British Aircraft Corporation">British Aircraft Corporation</a> (BAC)\xe2\x80\x94established a factory at the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although the de Havilland factory closed down in 1962 and aircraft manufacturing at Bournemouth Airport ceased by the late 1970s, the aircraft and engineering industries remained important to the local economy. The BAC works at Bournemouth Airport were converted into a 80-hectare (200-acre) industrial estate which has become one of the largest employment sites in the county with over 140 businesses and a working population of some 2,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The town has a number of smaller trading estates including: Airfield Way Industrial Estate, Sea Vixen Trading Estate, Silver Business Park, Hughes Business Park, Priory Park and Somerford Road, all situated on the old Christchurch Airfield; Fairmile/Avon Trading Park, once the old railway yard; and Groveley Road and Stony Lane.<sup id="cite_ref-Dorset_County_Council_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dorset_County_Council-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bournemouth Airport is among the busiest international airports in the country and is an important economic generator for the region.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Owned and operated by <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airports_Group" title="Manchester Airports Group">Manchester Airports Group</a>, the airport handles 800,000 passengers annually and supports around 900 full-time equivalent jobs which contribute more than \xc2\xa324&#160;million to the local economy.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Between 2007 and 2010 the airport underwent a \xc2\xa345&#160;million upgrade which included the construction of a new departure terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Other major employers in Christchurch include: <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems" title="BAE Systems">BAE Systems</a>, Bournemouth Aviation Services Company (BASCO), Beagle Aerospace, <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_Airport" title="Bournemouth Airport">Bournemouth International Airport Ltd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Channel_Express" title="Channel Express">Channel Express</a>, College of Air Traffic Control, Data Track Process Instruments, <a href="/wiki/European_Aviation_Air_Charter" title="European Aviation Air Charter">European Aviation</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=FR_Aviation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="FR Aviation (page does not exist)">FR Aviation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honeywell" title="Honeywell">Honeywell</a>, Reid Steel, Revvo Castor Company, <a href="/wiki/Sainsbury%27s" title="Sainsbury&#39;s">Sainsbury\'s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siemens_VAI" title="Siemens VAI">Siemens VAI</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=SELEX_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="SELEX Communications (page does not exist)">SELEX Communications</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dorset_County_Council_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dorset_County_Council-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The town\'s High Street contains 48 shops with 61,847 square feet (5,745.8&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of retail space.<sup id="cite_ref-retail_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-retail-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> The addition of the Saxon Square shopping precinct in 1982 added a further 41,748 square feet (3,878.5&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of shop floor to the town centre\xe2\x80\x94an increase of 67.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-retail_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-retail-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> The combined number of shops and floor space makes Christchurch the fifth largest shopping centre in Dorset.<sup id="cite_ref-retail_93-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-retail-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Christchurch attracts some 837,000 staying visitors and 792,000 day visitors each year and tourism generates \xc2\xa376,000,000 for the local economy.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\nAlthough important to the local economy with spending generating over \xc2\xa353,000,000 GVA, Christchurch is not so heavily dependent on tourism as some of its neighbours. Tourism\'s contribution to the local economy is about 9% compared to 18% for <a href="/wiki/Weymouth_and_Portland" title="Weymouth and Portland">Weymouth and Portland</a>, 15% for <a href="/wiki/Purbeck_(district)" class="mw-redirect" title="Purbeck (district)">Purbeck</a> and 12% for Bournemouth.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Visitor accommodation consists of 11 <a href="/wiki/Campsite" title="Campsite">caravan and camping parks</a> and some 900 bed spaces in eight hotels and 75 <a href="/wiki/Guest_house" title="Guest house">guest houses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bed_and_breakfast" title="Bed and breakfast">bed and breakfast</a> establishments.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Monday_Market_Christchurch_Dorset.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Monday_Market_Christchurch_Dorset.JPG/220px-Monday_Market_Christchurch_Dorset.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Monday_Market_Christchurch_Dorset.JPG/330px-Monday_Market_Christchurch_Dorset.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Monday_Market_Christchurch_Dorset.JPG/440px-Monday_Market_Christchurch_Dorset.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Monday_Market_Christchurch_Dorset.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Monday market, Christchurch High Street.</div></div></div>\n<p>A weekly market was granted to the town by <a href="/wiki/Baldwin_de_Redvers,_1st_Earl_of_Devon" title="Baldwin de Redvers, 1st Earl of Devon">Baldwin de Redvers</a> and the first market took place in 1149 at the junction of Castle Street and High Street.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> These weekly markets stopped in 1872 but resumed a century later in a car park next to the town hall, now the site of Saxon Square.<sup id="cite_ref-Taylor_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> When construction of the square began in 1983, the market was moved to a car park in Bank Close. Today it is held every Monday in High Street which is then closed to traffic. Periodically there are food fairs and a French market in the town.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Every year since 2000 the town has held a food and wine festival during May. It includes an international food market with over 100 stalls selling food and drink, and a large marquee with a kitchen area erected in Saxon Square. Here cooking demonstrations are given, sometimes by a celebrity chef: past guests have included <a href="/wiki/Gary_Rhodes" title="Gary Rhodes">Gary Rhodes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jean-Christophe_Novelli" title="Jean-Christophe Novelli">Jean-Christophe Novelli</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> The week-long festival is a community event which aims to educate people in healthy eating as well as the availability of foods. During the festival local chefs are invited into schools to demonstrate recipes; and throughout the weekend the marquee hosts a cookery workshop for 7\xe2\x80\x9310-year olds.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Christchurch holds an annual music festival on the first weekend in July. Originally a <a href="/wiki/Folk_music_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Folk music of England">folk festival</a>, the event has evolved to cater for a wider variety of tastes: <a href="/wiki/Clogging" title="Clogging">clog</a> and <a href="/wiki/Morris_dancing" class="mw-redirect" title="Morris dancing">morris dancing</a> groups and <a href="/wiki/Salsa_(dance)" title="Salsa (dance)">salsa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belly_dancing" class="mw-redirect" title="Belly dancing">belly dancing</a> exhibitions have featured. <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">Rock bands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul groups</a> have been included alongside the more traditional types of music. The festival\'s format changes annually but usually takes place on and around the town quay where a large marquee contains the main stage. Local bars often host smaller bands and dancing and exhibitions take place throughout the town centre.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another annual event is the <a href="/wiki/Regatta" title="Regatta">regatta</a> which has been held every year since 1909.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> It takes place around the second week in August and involves rowing competitions on the River Stour and a <a href="/wiki/Travelling_funfair" class="mw-redirect" title="Travelling funfair">travelling funfair</a> sited on the adjacent town <a href="/wiki/Quay" class="mw-redirect" title="Quay">quay</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">carnival</a> procession and large firework display takes place at the weekend. The part of the quay by the priory is known as <i>The Quomps</i> and was conveyed to the town in 1911 by <a href="/wiki/James_Harris,_5th_Earl_of_Malmesbury" title="James Harris, 5th Earl of Malmesbury">Lord Malmesbury</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> A 19th-century <a href="/wiki/Bandstand" title="Bandstand">bandstand</a> situated in the Quomps was an anonymous gift to the town in 1938.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> During the summer months it is used for free open-air concerts on Saturdays, one of the most popular being "Stompin\' on the Quomps", a <a href="/wiki/Smooth_jazz" title="Smooth jazz">smooth jazz</a> festival.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> On Sunday afternoons <a href="/wiki/Brass_band_(British_style)" class="mw-redirect" title="Brass band (British style)">brass bands</a> often play there.\n</p><p>The town has a museum: the <a href="/wiki/Red_House_Museum_and_Gardens,_Christchurch" title="Red House Museum and Gardens, Christchurch">Red House Museum</a> in Quay Road. Once the town\'s <a href="/wiki/Workhouse" title="Workhouse">workhouse</a>, the Red House contains permanent and temporary exhibitions pertaining to local history, costume, geology, natural history and archaeology. The museum grounds contain formal and informal gardens.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The old power station in Bargates, owned by <a href="/wiki/Scottish_and_Southern_Energy" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish and Southern Energy">Scottish and Southern Energy</a>, housed the Museum of Electricity. This is no longer open to the public, although the company is working on new ways to share the museum\'s collection more widely across the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Listed_buildings_in_Christchurch,_Dorset" title="Listed buildings in Christchurch, Dorset">Listed buildings in Christchurch, Dorset</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Town_centre">Town centre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Town centre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Town_Hall_Christchurch_Dorset.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Town_Hall_Christchurch_Dorset.JPG/220px-Town_Hall_Christchurch_Dorset.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Town_Hall_Christchurch_Dorset.JPG/330px-Town_Hall_Christchurch_Dorset.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Town_Hall_Christchurch_Dorset.JPG/440px-Town_Hall_Christchurch_Dorset.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Town_Hall_Christchurch_Dorset.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Mayor\'s Parlour and Saxon Square</div></div></div>\n<p>Christchurch\'s town centre encompasses a mixture of traditional public houses, restaurants, coffee shops, antiquated cottages and historic <a href="/wiki/Listed_buildings" class="mw-redirect" title="Listed buildings">listed buildings</a>. The older part of the town dates from Saxon times and retains its Saxon street layout.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The Grade II listed Mayor\'s Parlour was built as the market hall in 1745 at the far end of the High Street but was moved to its present position in 1849.<sup id="cite_ref-Hodges_p17_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hodges_p17-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> It was enclosed and extended, and used as the <a href="/wiki/Town_hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Town hall">town hall</a> until the civic offices were built in the mid-1970s. It was restored to its former condition circa 1982 when the Saxon Square shopping precinct was built.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>High Street contains two Grade II listed <a href="/wiki/Public_house" class="mw-redirect" title="Public house">public houses</a>: Ye Olde George Inne, once a <a href="/wiki/Coaching_inn" title="Coaching inn">coach house</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Hodges_p17_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hodges_p17-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> and the Ship Inn which has the oldest licence in Christchurch.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> A known haunt of <a href="/wiki/Smugglers" class="mw-redirect" title="Smugglers">smugglers</a>, the Ship Inn\'s history can be traced back to 1688.<sup id="cite_ref-Newman_1998_53_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newman_1998_53-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> At the end of High Street is Church Street which contains Church Hatch, a Grade II* listed <a href="/wiki/Georgian_architecture" title="Georgian architecture">Georgian</a> residence. Once the home of Sir <a href="/wiki/Owen_Tudor_Burne" title="Owen Tudor Burne">Owen Tudor Burne</a>, it was saved from demolition in 1929 by public appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Ye Olde Eight Bells, a Grade II listed gift shop in Church Street, was once another <a href="/wiki/Alehouse" class="mw-redirect" title="Alehouse">alehouse</a> frequented by smugglers and central to a number of local legends.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Close by in Castle Street is the Perfumery, a 14th-century <a href="/wiki/Thatched" class="mw-redirect" title="Thatched">thatched</a> property often referred to as the old courthouse; although some local historians maintain that this was next door and long gone.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The town centre contains three Grade I listed bridges. The Town Bridge is a 15th-century <a href="/wiki/Ashlar" title="Ashlar">ashlar</a> stone bridge composed of two portions separated by a narrow strip of land. The eastern portion crosses the narrower of two branches of the <a href="/wiki/River_Avon_(Hampshire)" class="mw-redirect" title="River Avon (Hampshire)">River Avon</a> that pass through the town and features five low round-headed <a href="/wiki/Arch" title="Arch">arches</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> The western bridge features two arches and crosses the millstream which runs adjacent to the Avon. To the east of the Town Bridge on the same route from the town centre the Waterloo Bridge spans the larger branch of the Avon. Built circa 1816\xe2\x80\x931817 in the mediaeval tradition with dressed <a href="/wiki/Portland_stone" title="Portland stone">Portland stone</a>, its design incorporates five wide segmental arches, circular piers and capped cutwaters.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> On the northern side of the bridge a modern steel pedestrian footbridge is cantilevered to the older structure.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Constable%27s_House_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1764117.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Constable%27s_House_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1764117.jpg/220px-Constable%27s_House_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1764117.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Constable%27s_House_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1764117.jpg/330px-Constable%27s_House_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1764117.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Constable%27s_House_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1764117.jpg/440px-Constable%27s_House_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1764117.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Constable%27s_House_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1764117.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Constable\'s House, a Grade I listed <a href="/wiki/Norman_architecture" title="Norman architecture">Norman</a> dwelling</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Castle">Castle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Castle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Grade I listed <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Castle" title="Christchurch Castle">Christchurch Castle</a> is of <a href="/wiki/Normans" title="Normans">Norman</a> origin and was originally of a <a href="/wiki/Motte_and_bailey" class="mw-redirect" title="Motte and bailey">motte and bailey</a> construction. The castle once dominated the town but now lies in ruins and only a couple of the <a href="/wiki/Keep" title="Keep">keep</a> walls remain. A castle has stood in Christchurch since approximately 924 AD when <a href="/wiki/Edward_the_Elder" title="Edward the Elder">Edward the Elder</a> fortified the town with a wooden fort on a <a href="/wiki/Motte" class="mw-redirect" title="Motte">motte</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Moxey_1997_87_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moxey_1997_87-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Norman_conquest" class="mw-redirect" title="Norman conquest">Norman conquest</a> in 1066 the castle\'s defences were strengthened with a ditch and <a href="/wiki/Motte-and-bailey" class="mw-redirect" title="Motte-and-bailey">bailey</a> surrounded by a wooden <a href="/wiki/Palisade" title="Palisade">palisade</a>. The wooden fort was replaced; at first with another wooden structure and then a stone keep which was constructed in the 12th century.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Moxey_1997_89_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moxey_1997_89-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Within the curtain wall of the castle stands the Constable\'s House, a Grade I listed <a href="/wiki/Norman_architecture" title="Norman architecture">Norman</a> dwelling. Much of the building\'s stonework remains, including a rare example of a Norman chimney (one of only five in the country) and the <a href="/wiki/Garderobe" title="Garderobe">privy</a> which extends out across the mill stream.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The castle was <a href="/wiki/Slighting" title="Slighting">slighted</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Roundhead" title="Roundhead">Parliamentary</a> army during the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a> to prevent the stronghold from falling into <a href="/wiki/Cavalier" title="Cavalier">Royalist</a> hands.<sup id="cite_ref-Moxey_1997_pp._89\xe2\x80\x9390_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moxey_1997_pp._89\xe2\x80\x9390-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stannard_p135/136_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stannard_p135/136-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Priory">Priory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Priory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Christchurch_Priory_-_geograph.org.uk_-_647546.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Christchurch_Priory_-_geograph.org.uk_-_647546.jpg/220px-Christchurch_Priory_-_geograph.org.uk_-_647546.jpg" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Christchurch_Priory_-_geograph.org.uk_-_647546.jpg/330px-Christchurch_Priory_-_geograph.org.uk_-_647546.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Christchurch_Priory_-_geograph.org.uk_-_647546.jpg/440px-Christchurch_Priory_-_geograph.org.uk_-_647546.jpg 2x" data-file-width="622" data-file-height="456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Christchurch_Priory_-_geograph.org.uk_-_647546.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Christchurch Priory dates from the 11th century</div></div></div>\n<p>Christchurch town centre and the Harbour are overlooked by the 11th century Grade I listed <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Priory" title="Christchurch Priory">Christchurch Priory</a>. Once a <a href="/wiki/Monastery" title="Monastery">monastery</a>, it was given to the town for use as a <a href="/wiki/Parish_church" title="Parish church">parish church</a> by <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry VIII">Henry VIII</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Monasteries" title="Dissolution of the Monasteries">dissolution</a> in 1540.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> It is the longest parish church in England with a <a href="/wiki/Nave" title="Nave">nave</a> over 311 feet (95&#160;m) long.<sup id="cite_ref-Moxey_1997_87_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moxey_1997_87-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> The nave and <a href="/wiki/Transepts" class="mw-redirect" title="Transepts">transepts</a> are Norman with heavy columns and round arches, whereas the <a href="/wiki/Lady_chapel" title="Lady chapel">lady chapel</a> is from the 14th century and more <a href="/wiki/Perpendicular_Period" class="mw-redirect" title="Perpendicular Period">Perpendicular</a> in style. The great <a href="/wiki/Choir_(architecture)" title="Choir (architecture)">choir</a> is even later, having been rebuilt in the 16th century. The Priory is noted for its <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Priory#Miraculous_beam" title="Christchurch Priory">Miraculous Beam</a>, which attracts pilgrims from all over the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Moxey_1997_87_122-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moxey_1997_87-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Within the Priory grounds stands Priory House, a Grade II listed mansion built in 1777 by <a href="/wiki/Gustavus_Brander" title="Gustavus Brander">Gustavus Brander</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hodges_2003_9_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hodges_2003_9-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> The Priory is in active use for worship and forms part of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Winchester" title="Diocese of Winchester">Diocese of Winchester</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Place_Mill">Place Mill</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Place Mill">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Place Mill is a Grade II* listed Anglo-Saxon <a href="/wiki/Watermill" title="Watermill">watermill</a> located a short distance to the south of the Priory on Christchurch Quay. It is mentioned in the <a href="/wiki/Domesday_Book" title="Domesday Book">Domesday Book</a> and features a mediaeval stone base underneath red brickwork.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> The mill belonged to the Priory but stopped working in 1908 and stood derelict until purchased by the council and restored in 1981. It is unique in that it takes water from one river (the <a href="/wiki/River_Avon_(Hampshire)" class="mw-redirect" title="River Avon (Hampshire)">Avon</a>) and spills it into a second river (the <a href="/wiki/River_Stour,_Dorset" title="River Stour, Dorset">Stour</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> A millstream is supplied from the <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Harbour#Royalty_Fishery" title="Christchurch Harbour">Royalty Fisheries</a> near to the Electricity Museum behind Bargates, and flows for nearly 0.5 miles (0.80&#160;km) to the mill between the Avon and the Priory grounds before joining the River Stour.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> A mediaeval Grade II listed bridge known as the Place Mill Bridge crosses the millstream nearby.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Highcliffe_Castle_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2029439.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Highcliffe_Castle_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2029439.jpg/220px-Highcliffe_Castle_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2029439.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Highcliffe_Castle_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2029439.jpg/330px-Highcliffe_Castle_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2029439.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Highcliffe_Castle_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2029439.jpg/440px-Highcliffe_Castle_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2029439.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Highcliffe_Castle_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2029439.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Highcliffe Castle, a Grade I listed mansion built between 1831 and 1835</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Highcliffe_Castle">Highcliffe Castle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Highcliffe Castle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Situated on the cliffs at <a href="/wiki/Highcliffe" title="Highcliffe">Highcliffe</a> is <a href="/wiki/Highcliffe_Castle" title="Highcliffe Castle">Highcliffe Castle</a>, a Grade I listed mansion.<sup id="cite_ref-listed_highcliffe_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-listed_highcliffe-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The building was designed by <a href="/wiki/William_Donthorne" title="William Donthorne">William Donthorne</a> for <a href="/wiki/Charles_Stuart,_1st_Baron_Stuart_de_Rothesay" title="Charles Stuart, 1st Baron Stuart de Rothesay">Charles Stuart, 1st Baron Stuart de Rothesay</a>, and built between 1831 and 1835. It stands on the site of "High Cliff", a demolished <a href="/wiki/Georgian_architecture" title="Georgian architecture">Georgian</a> mansion which belonged to Charles Stuart\'s grandfather <a href="/wiki/John_Stuart,_3rd_Earl_of_Bute" title="John Stuart, 3rd Earl of Bute">John Stuart, 3rd Earl of Bute</a>. An important remaining example of the <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">Gothic Revival</a> architecture, Donothorne\'s design incorporated French mediaeval stonework, <a href="/wiki/Stained_glass" title="Stained glass">stained glass</a> and 18th-century French <a href="/wiki/Panelling" title="Panelling">panelling</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_highcliffe_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph_highcliffe-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The house was sold in 1950 and was briefly used as a children\'s home and a Catholic <a href="/wiki/Seminary" title="Seminary">seminary</a>. After a devastating fire and years of neglect the castle was sold to Christchurch Borough Council in 1977 and underwent restoration.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Highcliffe Castle is open to the general public throughout the year and is used for weddings, private functions, exhibitions and other public events.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_and_recreation">Sports and recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sports and recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The town\'s <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> team, <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_F.C." title="Christchurch F.C.">Christchurch F.C.</a>, play at Hurn Bridge Sports Club situated at the junction of the Avon Causeway and Matchams Lane.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Established in 1885 the club was a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Hampshire_Football_Association" title="Hampshire Football Association">Hampshire Football Association</a> in 1887. Christchurch F.C. were promoted as champions to <a href="/wiki/Hampshire_League" title="Hampshire League">Hampshire League</a> One in 1938, 1948 and 1986, and in 1970, became the first team to win the Bournemouth Senior Cup three times in succession. The club joined the <a href="/wiki/Wessex_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Wessex League">Wessex League</a> (the ninth tier of the <a href="/wiki/English_football_league_system" title="English football league system">English football league system</a>) in 1988 and are one of the few clubs in the league that maintain amateur status.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hurn Bridge is also the home of Christchurch Cricket Club who have teams in the Saturday and Sunday Dorset Leagues.<sup id="cite_ref-cricket_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cricket-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> In 2009 the first XI won Division 3 having been newly promoted from Division 4. In those two seasons the team lost only four games.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Hurn Bridge houses the Dorset Cricket Centre, an indoor training facility run by the Dorset Cricket Board.<sup id="cite_ref-cricket_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cricket-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Christchurch has a council run <a href="/wiki/Leisure_centre" title="Leisure centre">leisure centre</a> situated at the end of Stony Lane South. The complex contains a swimming pool, golf course and indoor <a href="/wiki/Bowls" title="Bowls">bowling</a> facility which is home to the East Dorset Indoor Bowls Club.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> Christchurch has a lawn bowling club, Christchurch Bowling Club, that play on the green adjacent to the castle ruins.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> The town has two other lawn bowling clubs and golf courses; at Iford and Highcliffe.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sailing" title="Sailing">Sailing</a> is a popular leisure pursuit in Christchurch and the harbour is home to three sailing clubs: Highcliffe Sailing Club, Mudeford Sailing Club and Christchurch Sailing Club which are situated at Mudeford Quay, Fisherman\'s Bank and the Town Quay respectively. The other end of the Town Quay is home to the local <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">rowing</a> club.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Christchurch has some 199 kilometres (124&#160;mi) of highway of which 24 kilometres (15&#160;mi) are <a href="/wiki/A_roads_in_Great_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="A roads in Great Britain">A roads</a>, 32 kilometres (20&#160;mi) are <a href="/wiki/B_roads_in_Great_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="B roads in Great Britain">B and C roads</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> The town is served by the <a href="/wiki/A35_road" title="A35 road">A35 road</a> which runs from <a href="/wiki/Devon" title="Devon">Devon</a> through to <a href="/wiki/Southampton" title="Southampton">Southampton</a> via Poole, Bournemouth and the <a href="/wiki/New_Forest" title="New Forest">New Forest</a>. To the north of the town the A35 connects to the <a href="/wiki/A31_road" title="A31 road">A31</a>, the major trunk road in central southern England which provides access to the <a href="/wiki/M27_motorway" title="M27 motorway">M27 motorway</a> at Southampton. The <a href="/wiki/A338_road" title="A338 road">A338 road</a> runs northwards from Bournemouth through Christchurch to <a href="/wiki/Ringwood" title="Ringwood">Ringwood</a> in Hampshire.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Two bus companies operate within the borough: <a href="/wiki/Wilts_%26_Dorset" title="Wilts &amp; Dorset">Wilts &amp; Dorset</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Buses" title="Yellow Buses">Yellow Buses</a>. Together they provide direct routes from Christchurch to: <a href="/wiki/Alderney,_Dorset" title="Alderney, Dorset">Alderney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beaulieu,_Hampshire" title="Beaulieu, Hampshire">Beaulieu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boscombe" title="Boscombe">Boscombe</a>, Bournemouth, <a href="/wiki/Burley,_Hampshire" title="Burley, Hampshire">Burley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burton,_Dorset" title="Burton, Dorset">Burton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Highcliffe" title="Highcliffe">Highcliffe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lymington" title="Lymington">Lymington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milford_on_Sea" title="Milford on Sea">Milford on Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mudeford" title="Mudeford">Mudeford</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Milton" title="New Milton">New Milton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parkstone" title="Parkstone">Parkstone</a>, Poole, <a href="/wiki/Ringwood" title="Ringwood">Ringwood</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Westbourne,_Dorset" title="Westbourne, Dorset">Westbourne</a>. During the summer months, it is possible to travel directly to <a href="/wiki/Chichester" title="Chichester">Chichester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dorchester,_Dorset" title="Dorchester, Dorset">Dorchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hedge_End" title="Hedge End">Hedge End</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paultons_Park" title="Paultons Park">Paultons Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth" title="Portsmouth">Portsmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salisbury" title="Salisbury">Salisbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southsea" title="Southsea">Southsea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Weymouth,_Dorset" title="Weymouth, Dorset">Weymouth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Christchurch_railway_station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1762827.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Christchurch_railway_station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1762827.jpg/220px-Christchurch_railway_station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1762827.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Christchurch_railway_station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1762827.jpg/330px-Christchurch_railway_station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1762827.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Christchurch_railway_station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1762827.jpg/440px-Christchurch_railway_station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1762827.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Christchurch_railway_station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1762827.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Christchurch_railway_station,_Dorset" class="mw-redirect" title="Christchurch railway station, Dorset">Christchurch railway station</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Christchurch_railway_station,_Dorset" class="mw-redirect" title="Christchurch railway station, Dorset">Christchurch railway station</a> is on the <a href="/wiki/South_Western_Main_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="South Western Main Line">South Western Main Line</a> from <a href="/wiki/London_Waterloo_station" title="London Waterloo station">London Waterloo</a> to <a href="/wiki/Weymouth_railway_station" title="Weymouth railway station">Weymouth</a>. Services are operated by <a href="/wiki/South_West_Trains" title="South West Trains">South West Trains</a> and depart for London Waterloo twice an hour, Monday to Saturday; and hourly on Sunday.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Weymouth, Dorchester, Wareham, Poole, Bournemouth, Brockenhurst, Southampton and its airport, Eastleigh, Winchester, Basingstoke, Farnborough, Woking, Waterloo can be accessed directly from Christchurch station.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_Airport" title="Bournemouth Airport">Bournemouth Airport</a> is situated in <a href="/wiki/Hurn" title="Hurn">Hurn</a> (a small village within the Christchurch Borough boundary) and is around 3.75 miles (6.04&#160;km) north-west of Christchurch town centre. Originally an <a href="/wiki/RAF_Hurn" title="RAF Hurn">RAF airfield</a>, the airport began commercial services in the late 1950s and now serves around 800,000 passengers annually.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>, <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thomson_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomson Airways">Thomson Airways</a> operate from the airport and provide scheduled flights to European destinations.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the summer months small passenger <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">ferries</a> travel between Tuckton and Mudeford Spit via the town quay.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Another ferry crosses the Stour between <a href="/wiki/Wick,_Bournemouth" title="Wick, Bournemouth">Wick</a> and the Quay just below Tuckton Bridge. This <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://digitalcollections.qut.edu.au/4297/">ferry</a> was running before the bridge was built in 1882 and was then, the only crossing below Iford.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>Another ferry service operates across the harbour entrance from Mudeford Sandbank to Mudeford Quay. This ferry was operated by rowing boats until the 1960s; payment being at the discretion of the passenger.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Christchurch has two <a href="/wiki/Infant_school" title="Infant school">infant schools</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Junior_school" title="Junior school">junior schools</a>, five <a href="/wiki/Primary_school" title="Primary school">primary schools</a> (combined infant and junior) and three <a href="/wiki/Secondary_school" title="Secondary school">secondary schools</a>. The secondary schools are, in order of size: <a href="/wiki/Twynham_School" title="Twynham School">Twynham School</a> (1,515 pupils), <a href="/wiki/Highcliffe_School" title="Highcliffe School">Highcliffe School</a> (1,347 pupils) and <a href="/wiki/The_Grange_School,_Christchurch" title="The Grange School, Christchurch">the Grange School</a> (637 pupils). The secondary schools share a <a href="/wiki/Sixth_form" title="Sixth form">sixth form</a> with the three sites providing different courses.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Schools in Christchurch fall under the jurisdiction of Dorset County Council. From the 2008 <a href="/wiki/General_Certificate_of_Secondary_Education" title="General Certificate of Secondary Education">General Certificate of Secondary Education</a> (GCSE) results, Dorset was ranked 32nd out of 148 local authorities in England based on the percentage of pupils attaining at least five A* to C grades at GCSE level including maths and English.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Twynham was the best performing school in Christchurch in 2009: 67% of pupils gained five or more GCSEs at A* to C grade including maths and English compared to the national average of 49.8%.<sup id="cite_ref-GCSE_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCSE-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Highcliffe achieved 62% but the Grange School was less successful: only 40% of pupils achieved five or more A* to C grade results.<sup id="cite_ref-GCSE_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCSE-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Twynham was also the best performing school for <a href="/wiki/GCE_Advanced_Level" title="GCE Advanced Level">A-level</a> results with an average score of 727.8 points per student, slightly below the national average of 739.3.<sup id="cite_ref-A_level_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_level-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Highcliffe School School students averaged 618.4 points and the Grange School 571.9 points.<sup id="cite_ref-A_level_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_level-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_residents">Notable residents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Notable residents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:3rd_Earl_of_Bute_by_Sir_Joshua_Reynolds.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/3rd_Earl_of_Bute_by_Sir_Joshua_Reynolds.jpg/170px-3rd_Earl_of_Bute_by_Sir_Joshua_Reynolds.jpg" width="170" height="277" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/3rd_Earl_of_Bute_by_Sir_Joshua_Reynolds.jpg/255px-3rd_Earl_of_Bute_by_Sir_Joshua_Reynolds.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/3rd_Earl_of_Bute_by_Sir_Joshua_Reynolds.jpg/340px-3rd_Earl_of_Bute_by_Sir_Joshua_Reynolds.jpg 2x" data-file-width="491" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:3rd_Earl_of_Bute_by_Sir_Joshua_Reynolds.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/John_Stuart,_3rd_Earl_of_Bute" title="John Stuart, 3rd Earl of Bute">John Stuart, 3rd Earl of Bute</a>, Prime Minister between 1762\xe2\x80\x9363, owned a mansion house in Christchurch</div></div></div>\n<p>Christchurch has been the birthplace and home of notable people including <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Ferrey" title="Benjamin Ferrey">Benjamin Ferrey</a>, a renowned architect who was one of the earliest members of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Institute_of_British_Architects" title="Royal Institute of British Architects">Royal Institute of British Architects</a>, of which he was twice Vice-President, and a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Gold_Medal" title="Royal Gold Medal">Royal Gold Medallist</a> in 1870. Ferrey\'s works include the restorations of Christchurch Priory and <a href="/wiki/Wells_Cathedral" title="Wells Cathedral">Wells Cathedral</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Lyons,_1st_Baron_Lyons" title="Edmund Lyons, 1st Baron Lyons">Edmund Lyons</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> admiral and diplomat who was born and lived in the parish of Burton. He served in the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> and was elevated to the <a href="/wiki/Peerage" title="Peerage">peerage</a> in 1856 as <a href="/wiki/Viscount_Lyons" title="Viscount Lyons">Baron Lyons, of Christchurch in the County of Southampton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Gustavus_Brander" title="Gustavus Brander">Gustavus Brander</a>, curator at the <a href="/wiki/British_Museum" title="British Museum">British Museum</a> and governor of the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_England" title="Bank of England">Bank of England</a> lived at Priory House which he had built in 1777 in the grounds of Christchurch Priory. <a href="/wiki/Louis-Phillipe" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis-Phillipe">Prince Louis Phillipe</a>, the future King of France took refuge there during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hodges_2003_9_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hodges_2003_9-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Southey" title="Robert Southey">Robert Southey</a>, writer, poet and <a href="/wiki/Poet_Laureate" class="mw-redirect" title="Poet Laureate">Poet Laureate</a>; lived in Burton between 1797 and 1799. Many other writers and poets of the day visited him there including his brother in law, poet <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Coleridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Samuel Coleridge">Samuel Coleridge</a>, and the Scottish novelist and poet <a href="/wiki/Sir_Walter_Scott" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Walter Scott">Sir Walter Scott</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/John_Stuart,_3rd_Earl_of_Bute" title="John Stuart, 3rd Earl of Bute">John Stuart, 3rd Earl of Bute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Great_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister of Great Britain">Prime Minister</a> 1762\xe2\x80\x9363, amateur <a href="/wiki/Botany" title="Botany">botanist</a> and one of the founders of <a href="/wiki/Royal_Botanic_Gardens,_Kew" title="Royal Botanic Gardens, Kew">Royal Botanic Gardens, Kew</a>; built a mansion, High Cliff House, on his Christchurch estate close to the cliff top in 1773.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_highcliffe_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph_highcliffe-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The area is now known as <a href="/wiki/Highcliffe" title="Highcliffe">Highcliffe</a>. <a href="/wiki/Charles_Stuart,_1st_Baron_Stuart_de_Rothesay" title="Charles Stuart, 1st Baron Stuart de Rothesay">Charles Stuart, 1st Baron Stuart de Rothesay</a>, diplomat and grandson of John Stuart, 3rd Earl of Bute; built <a href="/wiki/Highcliffe_Castle" title="Highcliffe Castle">Highcliffe Castle</a> a grand, <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">romantic style</a> mansion house on the site of his grandfather\'s house.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_highcliffe_133-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph_highcliffe-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/George_Rose_(Treasurer_of_the_Navy)" class="mw-redirect" title="George Rose (Treasurer of the Navy)">Sir George Rose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">Member of Parliament</a> for <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Christchurch (UK Parliament constituency)">Christchurch</a> and close friend and advisor to the Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/William_Pitt_the_Younger" title="William Pitt the Younger">William Pitt</a>, built a home, \'Sandhills\', at Mudeford. His other great friend, <a href="/wiki/King_George_III" class="mw-redirect" title="King George III">King George III</a> often visited, helping to promote Christchurch as a tourist destination.<sup id="cite_ref-Hodges_2003_p._116_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hodges_2003_p._116-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Sandhills was home to George Rose\'s two sons: politician and diplomat <a href="/wiki/George_Henry_Rose" title="George Henry Rose">Sir George Henry Rose</a>, and poet <a href="/wiki/William_Stewart_Rose" title="William Stewart Rose">William Rose</a>, who both served as Members of Parliament for Christchurch.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Rose,_1st_Baron_Strathnairn" title="Hugh Rose, 1st Baron Strathnairn">Field Marshal Hugh Rose, 1st Baron Strathnairn</a>, son of Sir George Henry Rose spent time living at the family home.<sup id="cite_ref-Powell_1995_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Powell_1995-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>James Clark (1825-1890), horticulturist and early genetic hybridist who specialised in breeding new potato varieties. He was born in Wick near <a href="/wiki/Tuckton" title="Tuckton">Tuckton</a> (then a part of Christchurch) and lived his whole life in the Christchurch area. In response to the <a href="/wiki/Great_Famine_(Ireland)" title="Great Famine (Ireland)">Irish Potato Famine</a> he developed the Magnum Bonum potato, which is widely acknowledged as the first disease resistant variety. Magnum Bonum was trialled by entrepreneurial horticulturalist <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Hibberd" title="Shirley Hibberd">Shirley Hibberd</a> and subsequently sold to <a href="/wiki/Suttons_Seeds" title="Suttons Seeds">Sutton\'s Seeds</a>, who introduced it in 1876. Clark later developed many other varieties of potato, of which Epicure is still grown.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sir_Donald_Bailey" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Donald Bailey">Sir Donald Bailey</a>, a civil engineer, developed the <a href="/wiki/Bailey_bridge" title="Bailey bridge">Bailey bridge</a> while he worked in Christchurch during the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>. Bailey lived in Christchurch after he retired in 1966 until his death in 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-Stannard_1999_241_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stannard_1999_241-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Former <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England football international</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> player <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Redknapp" title="Jamie Redknapp">Jamie Redknapp</a> attended <a href="/wiki/Twynham_School" title="Twynham School">Twynham School</a> when his father, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Redknapp" title="Harry Redknapp">Harry Redknapp</a>, managed <a href="/wiki/A.F.C._Bournemouth" title="A.F.C. Bournemouth">A.F.C. Bournemouth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Another footballer, retired <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a> goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Bob_Wilson_(footballer_born_1941)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bob Wilson (footballer born 1941)">Bob Wilson</a>, has a home near the town centre.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns">Twin towns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christchurch,_Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit
